<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Je pense que vous trouverez ce blog utile pour comprendre le d√©ploiement d‚Äôapplications et la configuration de la base de donn√©es sur l‚Äôapplication sur Kubernetes.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Dans ce didacticiel, nous aborderons les concepts essentiels des </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">biblioth√®ques partag√©es Jenkins</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> et fournirons un guide pratique pour la cr√©ation de biblioth√®ques partag√©es pour les pipelines.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Nous vivons √† l'√®re des microservices, o√π les applications modernes sont divis√©es en composants d√©ployables individuellement. Contrairement √† une application monolithique, vous pouvez disposer de plusieurs pipelines pour d√©ployer chaque microservice.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">De plus, Jenkins est utilis√© pour le d√©veloppement et le d√©ploiement d'infrastructures en tant que code.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Avec </font></font><a data-id="5002" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/jenkins-pipeline-as-code/"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">le pipeline Jenkins en tant que code</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> , nous pouvons coder l'int√©gralit√© de notre processus CI/CD. Il est trait√© de la m√™me mani√®re que nous d√©veloppons le code d'application. Vous pouvez versionner votre code de pipeline et effectuer tous les niveaux de test avant de l'utiliser pour tout d√©ploiement d'application.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Cependant, nous pouvons avoir des pipelines r√©utilisables bien d√©finis en utilisant la biblioth√®que partag√©e Jenkins.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Lorsque nous parlons de CI/CD en tant que code, il doit √™tre modulaire et r√©utilisable. Et surtout, il doit suivre les </font></font><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don't_repeat_yourself" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">principes DRY</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> (Don't Repeat Yourself). C'est l√† que la biblioth√®que partag√©e Jenkins entre en jeu.</font></font></p>
<p><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Biblioth√®que partag√©e</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> ‚Äì Comme son nom l‚Äôindique, il s‚Äôagit d‚Äôune biblioth√®que qui peut √™tre partag√©e.</font></font></p>
<p><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">La biblioth√®que partag√©e Jenkins</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> est le concept d'avoir un code de pipeline commun dans le syst√®me de contr√¥le de version qui peut √™tre utilis√© par n'importe quel nombre de pipelines simplement en le r√©f√©ren√ßant. En fait, </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">plusieurs √©quipes</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> peuvent utiliser la m√™me biblioth√®que pour leurs pipelines.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Vous pouvez le comparer √† la </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">biblioth√®que de programmation commune</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> . En programmation, nous cr√©ons des biblioth√®ques individuelles qui peuvent √™tre utilis√©es par n'importe qui en les important simplement dans son code.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Supposons que vous ayez dix pipelines de microservices Java, l' </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">√©tape de construction Maven</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> est dupliqu√©e sur les dix pipelines. Et chaque fois qu'un nouveau service est ajout√©, vous devrez copier et coller √† nouveau le code du pipeline. Maintenant, disons que vous souhaitez modifier certains param√®tres dans l'√©tape de construction Maven. Vous devrez le modifier manuellement dans tous les pipelines.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Pour </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">√©viter la duplication du code du pipeline</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> , nous pouvons √©crire une biblioth√®que partag√©e pour la construction Maven, et dans tous les pipelines, nous devons simplement faire r√©f√©rence au code de la biblioth√®que de construction Maven.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">√Ä l'avenir, pour toute modification de build Maven, il vous suffira de mettre √† jour le code de la biblioth√®que partag√©e. Les modifications seront ensuite appliqu√©es √† tous les pipelines utilisant la biblioth√®que de build Maven.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Dans l‚Äôensemble, la biblioth√®que partag√©e Jenkins r√©pond aux probl√®mes suivants.</font></font></p>
<p>The Jenkins shared library examples used in this guide are hosted on a <a href="https://github.com/techiescamp/jenkins-shared-library" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">GitHub Repository.</a> </p>
<p>Clone the repository to follow along with the guide.</p>
<p>A shared library is a collection of <strong>Groovy files (DSLs + Groovy)</strong>. All the Groovy files <strong>should be present in a git repo.</strong></p>
<p>In this example, we will be using Github as our Git repo.¬†</p>
<p>You can clone this repo to get the basic structure of the shared library.</p>
<p>The shared library repo has the following folder structure.</p>
<p>Let‚Äôs understand what each folder means.</p>
<p>This directory holds all the <strong>global shared library code</strong> that can be called from a Jenkins pipeline. It holds all the library files with a .<strong>groovy</strong> extension. </p>
<p>Here is a simple library code for Git checkout. </p>
<p><strong>Don‚Äôt worry about the syntax</strong>. We can generate it using the Jenkins pipeline generator. We will look at it practically in the following sections.</p>
<p>The vars directory also supports <strong>.txt</strong> files for the documentation of shared library code. </p>
<p>For example, if you have a file named <strong>maven-build<g class="gr_ gr_392 gr-alert gr_gramm gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim Style replaceWithoutSep" data-gr-id="392" id="392">.groovy</g></strong>, you can have a helper file named <strong>maven-groovy.txt</strong>. In this file, you can write the respective shared library function help documentation in markdown format.¬† The help file can be viewed from¬†<strong>&lt;your-jenkins-url&gt;/pipeline-syntax/globals</strong> page.¬†</p>
<p>It is a¬†regular Java source directory. Here you can add mode complex and object-oriented code Groovy code to extend your shared library code. Also, you can<strong> import core Jenkins and its plugin classes</strong> using an import statement.</p>
<p>You might ask, when we have a vars directory, what is the <strong>need for src?</strong></p>
<p>There are scenarios where the <strong>groovy DSLs will not be flexible enough</strong> to achieve some complex functionalities. In this case, you can write custom Groovy functions in src and call them in your shared library code.</p>
<p>The src directory is added to the classpath during every script compilation. So we can <strong>directly use the classes</strong> defined in the <code>src</code> directory in Jenkinsfiles.</p>
<p>All the <strong>non-groovy files</strong> (e.g., text files, templates) required for your pipelines can be managed in this folder. Typically files.</p>
<p>One such example is, you might¬†need a common JSON template to make an API call during the build. This JSON template can be stored in the resources folder and can be accessed in the shared library using the¬†<code><strong>libraryResource</strong></code>¬†function.</p>
<p>Or You can use a <strong>HTML file as a template</strong> for sending HTML-formatted email notifications from your Jenkins pipelines. In your pipeline script or shared library function, you can load this template and replace the placeholders with actual values.</p>
<p>We will look into the following four things to get your hands dirty with the shared library.</p>
<p>Let‚Äôs look at each one in detail.</p>
<p><em><strong>Note:</strong> In this guide, we will concentrate only on the vars folder for creating your first shared library. The advanced shared library guide will cover src and resources.</em></p>
<p>Jenkins shared library has the following structure. You can get the basic structure and code used in this article from Github -&gt; <a aria-label="Structure de la biblioth√®que partag√©e Jenkins (s'ouvre dans un nouvel onglet)" href="https://github.com/devopscube/jenkins-shared-library-structure.git" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">Jenkins Shared Library Structure</a></p>
<p>All the files under vars are <strong>global functions and variables</strong>. The file name is the function name. We will be using the filename in our declarative pipeline.</p>

<p>Like <strong><code>gitCheckout</code></strong>, you can create all your pipeline steps a shared library and you don‚Äôt have to repeat your common functionalities in all your pipelines.</p>
<p><strong><code>@Library('jenkins-shared-library@master') _</code></strong> tells Jenkins to use the globally configured library named <strong><code>jenkins-shared-library</code></strong>.</p>
<p>When you use this import statement, Jenkins will fetch the shared library code from the configured source (typically a Git repository) and make it available for use in your pipeline.</p>
<p>In larger enterprises, it is common to have central platform teams.</p>
<p>If Jenkins is used in such organizations, these platform teams usually create common Jenkins libraries for all application and infrastructure deployment tasks.</p>
<p>Application teams can reuse these pipelines to save time. Since these libraries are extensible, if the common libraries don‚Äôt meet the specific project needs, they can always be customized.</p>
<p>It is also common practice for teams to contribute to the central platform teams‚Äô shared libraries. This way, organizations can maintain efficient and streamlined pipeline libraries.</p>
<p>As I have explained in many other blogs, unit testing is important for Infrastructure as code. </p>
<p>Not every team writes tests, however, unit testing shared libraries is<strong> an important best practice in Jenkins pipeline development</strong>. It ensures code reliability, catches bugs early, and facilitates safe refactoring. </p>
<p>By thoroughly testing shared library functions, teams can prevent widespread issues across multiple pipelines, as these libraries often form the backbone of an organization‚Äôs CI/CD processes. </p>
<p>Writing unit test requires <strong>familiarity with Java, Groovy and JUnit testing framework</strong>. Usually central platform team will have dedicated resources to write these tests for all the shared library functions.</p>
<p>In essence, although it takes time and effort, unit testing shared libraries is an investment in the stability, maintainability, and efficiency of your entire CI/CD ecosystem.</p>
<p>If you are using Jenkins for your CI/CD needs, implementing a shared library is a must.</p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Il simplifie votre flux de travail CI/CD avec Jenkins. Le meilleur, c'est que vous pouvez disposer d'un flux de travail de d√©veloppement bien d√©fini pour d√©velopper et tester le code du pipeline Jenkins.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Si vous avez des questions concernant les biblioth√®ques partag√©es, faites-le nous savoir dans la section commentaires.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Il est tr√®s important d'avoir une sauvegarde de Jenkins avec ses donn√©es et ses configurations. Cela comprend les configurations de t√¢ches, les journaux de builds, les plugins, la configuration des plugins, etc.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Jenkins n√©cessite des correctifs et des mises √† jour de plugins r√©guliers. Au cours de ces processus, il existe un risque de probl√®mes de configuration, qui peuvent potentiellement conduire √† un crash de Jenkins.</font></font></p>

<p>Note: You cannot use the Docker hub images directly due to security compliance issues in actual projects. Sou you have to build your own Docker images and host them in the organization-approved container registry.</p>
<p>It is better to attach a shared persistent volume to the build container to speed up the build process.</p>
<p>For example, if you take a Java application, it has many Maven package dependencies.</p>
<p>When you build the Java apps, it downloads dependencies added in the pom.xml from the remote maven repository the first time, and it creates a local .m2 cache directory where the dependent packages are cached.</p>
<p>The <code>.m2</code> cache is impossible in Docker agent-based builds as it gets destroyed after the build.</p>
<p>To solve this issue, we can create a persistent volume for the maven cache and attach it to the agent pod via the container template.</p>
<p>To demonstrate this, first, let‚Äôs create a PVC</p>
<p>Here is an example <code>Jenkinsfile</code> with a POD template that uses the <code>maven-repo-storage</code> persistent volume.</p>
<p>If you are using Docker to deploy applications, you can integrate your CI Docker build pipeline with Kubernetes agents.</p>
<p>There are a few ways to <a data-id="https://devopscube.com/run-docker-in-docker/" data-type="URL" href="https://devopscube.com/run-docker-in-docker/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">run </a><span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;"><a href="https://devopscube.com/run-docker-in-docker/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Docker on Docker</a>¬†for build use cases. However, since Kubernetes removed Docker</span> runtimes, it is better to use alternative solutions.</p>
<p>For now, the best way to build docker images on the Kubernetes cluster is using <a data-id="https://github.com/GoogleContainerTools/kaniko" data-type="URL" href="https://github.com/GoogleContainerTools/kaniko" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">Kaniko</a></p>
<p>Refer <a data-id="https://devopscube.com/build-docker-image-kubernetes-pod/" data-type="URL" href="https://devopscube.com/build-docker-image-kubernetes-pod/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">building docker image using kaniko </a>to learn more about kaniko build pipeline using Jenkins pipeline.</p>
<p>If you are using Jenkins &amp; Kubernetes, you should definitely try out the container-based agents.</p>
<p>Scaling your Jenkins agents on Kubernetes helps you avoid the administrative overhead associated with static build VMs. Even though dynamic VM build options are available, each build could take a long time compared to dynamic container agents.</p>
<p>You don‚Äôt have to worry about running out of resources for Jenkins builds. </p>

<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Il n‚Äôexiste aucun moyen direct de configurer Jenkins en mode haute disponibilit√© en raison de la fa√ßon dont Jenkins g√®re ses donn√©es.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Jenkins g√®re ses </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">donn√©es dans un fichier plat (xml)</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> et vous ne pouvez avoir qu'une seule instance du n≈ìud ma√Ætre qui peut lire les donn√©es Jenkins.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Pour cette raison, l'ex√©cution de plusieurs r√©pliques du </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">ma√Ætre Jenkins dans une configuration active-active</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> (o√π toutes les r√©pliques traitent activement des t√¢ches) n'est pas officiellement prise en charge.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Par exemple, si vous essayez de configurer plusieurs n≈ìuds ma√Ætres avec un volume partag√©, vous aurez des lectures et des √©critures incoh√©rentes qui conduiront √† un Jenkins instable.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Il existe deux fa√ßons d'avoir Jenkins en mode HA.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Vous pouvez appeler cette m√©thode une </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">solution de pauvre pour Jenkins HA.</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> Car, lorsqu'une instance tombe en panne, il y a quelques minutes d'indisponibilit√© pour qu'une autre instance se r√©tablisse (temps de d√©marrage de la machine virtuelle + service Java). Mais √ßa marche üôÇ</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Cette m√©thode fonctionnera sur n‚Äôimporte quelle plateforme cloud priv√©e/publique avec l‚Äôoption de mise √† l‚Äô√©chelle automatique.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Cette m√©thode est similaire au </font></font><a data-id="https://devopscube.com/setup-jenkins-on-kubernetes-cluster/" data-type="URL" href="https://devopscube.com/setup-jenkins-on-kubernetes-cluster/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">d√©ploiement de Jenkins sur Kubernetes</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> , o√π si le pod Jenkins tombe en panne, un autre pod g√©n√©rera les m√™mes donn√©es.¬†</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Au lieu d'un pod, il s'agit d'une machine virtuelle, donc le temps de d√©marrage prend plus de temps que le lancement d'un nouveau pod.</font></font></p>

<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Par exemple, si vous souhaitez </font></font><a data-id="15131" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/backup-etcd-restore-kubernetes/"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">sauvegarder etcd,</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> vous devez conna√Ætre le point de terminaison du service etcd et les certificats associ√©s pour vous authentifier aupr√®s d'etcd et cr√©er une sauvegarde.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Si vous ouvrez le </font></font><strong><code>etcd.yaml</code></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">manifeste, vous pouvez afficher toutes les configurations li√©es √† etcd comme indiqu√© ci-dessous.</font></font></p>
<p>In Kubernetes, all the components talk to each other over mTLS. Under the PKI folder, you will find all the TLS certificates and keys. Kubernetes control plane components use these certificates to authenticate and communicate with each other.</p>
<p>Also, there is an etcd subdirectory that contains the etcd-specific certificates and private keys. These are used to secure communication between etcd nodes and between the API server and etcd nodes.</p>
<p>The following image shows the file structure of the PKI folder.</p>
<p>The static pod manifests refer to the required TLS certificates and keys from this folder.</p>
<p>When you work on a self-hosted cluster using tools like kubeadm, these certificates are automatically generated by the tool. In managed kubernetes clusters, the cloud provider takes care of all the TLS requirements as it is their responsibility to manage control plane components. </p>
<p>However, if you are setting up a self-hosted cluster for production use, these certificates have to be requested from the organization‚Äôs network or security team. They will generate these certificates signed by the organization‚Äôs internal Certificate authority and provide them to you.</p>
<p>Any components that need to authenticate to the API server need the <a data-id="13806" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/kubernetes-kubeconfig-file/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">kubeconfig file</a>.</p>
<p>All the cluster Kubeconfig files are present in the <code><strong>/etc/kubernetes</strong></code> folder (.conf files). You will find the following files.</p>
<p>It contains the API server endpoint, cluster CA certificate, cluster client certificate, and other information. </p>
<p>The <strong><code>admin.conf,</code></strong> file, which is the admin kubeconfig file used by end users to access the API server to manage the clusters. You can use this file to connect the cluster from a remote workstation.</p>
<p>The Kubeconfig for the Controller manager, scheduler, and Kubelet is used for API server authentication and authorization.</p>
<p>For example, if you check the Controller Manager static pod manifest file, you can see the <strong><code>controller-manager.conf</code></strong> added as the authentication and authorization parameter.</p>
<p>Kubelet service runs as a systems service on all the cluster nodes.</p>
<p>You can view the kubelet systemd service under<strong><code> /etc/systemd/system/kubelet.service.d</code></strong></p>
<p>Here are the system file contents. </p>
<p>I have highlighted two important kubelet configurations in bold.</p>
<p>The kubeconfig file will be used for API server authentication and authorization.</p>
<p>The <strong>/var/lib/kubelet/config.yaml</strong> contains all the kubelet-related configurations. The static pod manifest location is added as part of the <strong>staticPodPath</strong> parameter. </p>
<p><strong>/var/lib/kubelet/kubeadm-flags.env</strong> file contains the container runtime environment Linux socket and the infra container (pause container) image. </p>
<p>For example, here is the kubelet config that is using the CRI-O container runtime, as indicated by the Unix socket and the pause container image.</p>
<p>A pause container is a minimal container that is the first to be started within a Kubernetes Pod. Then the role of the pause container is to hold the networking namespace and other shared resources for all the other containers in the same Pod.</p>
<p>If you look at the kubelet configuration in the managed k8s cluster, it looks a little different than the kubeadm setup.</p>
<p>For example, here is a kubelet service file for an <a data-id="15728" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/create-aws-eks-cluster-eksctl/">AWS EKS cluster</a>.</p>
<p>Here you can see the container runtime is containerd and its Unix socket flag is directly added to the service file</p>
<p>The kubelet kubeconfig file is in a different directory as compared to kubeadm configurations.</p>
<p><a data-id="https://coredns.io/" data-type="URL" href="https://coredns.io/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">CoreDNS</a> addon components deal with the cluster DNS configurations.</p>
<p>All the CoreDNS configurations are part of a configmap named CoreDNS in the kubesystem namespace.</p>
<p>If you list the <strong><code>Configmaps</code></strong> in the kube-system namespace, you can see the CoreDNS configmap.</p>
<p>use the following command to view the <strong>CoreDNS</strong> configmap contents.</p>

<p>When it comes to DNS connectivity, applications may need to connect to:</p>

<p>For example, let‚Äôs say the custom DNS server IP is <strong>10.45.45.34</strong> and your DNS suffix is <strong>dns-onprem.com</strong>, we have to add a block as shown below. So that all the DNS requests related to that domain endpoint will be forwarded to <strong>10.45.45.34</strong> DNS server.</p>

<p>When it comes to production clusters, audit logging is a must-have feature.</p>
<p>Audit logging is enabled in the <strong><code>kube-api-server.yaml</code></strong> static pod manifest.</p>
<p>The command argument should have the following two parameters. The file path is arbitrary and it depends on the cluster administrator.</p>

<p>When it comes to self-hosted Kubernetes clusters, which primarily happen in on-premise environments, you need to know each and every configuration of the cluster control plane and the worker nodes.</p>

<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">DRY ‚Äì ¬´ Ne vous r√©p√©tez pas ¬ª</font></font></p>

<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Par exemple, </font></font><a data-id="1976" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/jenkins-shared-library-tutorial/"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">la biblioth√®que partag√©e Jenkins</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> et les workflows communs GitHub Actions vous permettent de r√©utiliser les workflows existants pour les pipelines.</font></font></p>
<p><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Remarque</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">¬†: il est parfois difficile de d√©velopper des modules communs qui r√©pondent √† toutes les exigences. <p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Nous sommes dans l'√®re de GitOps.</font></font></p>

<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Ne cr√©ez pas ou ne d√©clenchez pas manuellement de pipelines, du moins pendant le d√©veloppement. <p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Le d√©ploiement dans des environnements sp√©cifiques tels que la pr√©paration ou la production </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">peut n√©cessiter une intervention manuelle</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> . <p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Par exemple, une modification de code peut n√©cessiter l‚Äôapprobation des √©quipes d‚Äôassurance qualit√©, des √©quipes de performance, des √©quipes de s√©curit√© et des parties prenantes de l‚Äôentreprise avant d‚Äô√™tre d√©ploy√©e dans un environnement de production.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Lorsque nous utilisons des outils CI/CD dans un r√©seau ouvert, nous pouvons acc√©der √† toutes les ressources disponibles en ligne, et vous pouvez les t√©l√©charger et les utiliser √† tout moment.</font></font></p>
<p>However, in real projects, CI/CD tools are set up in a private network behind forward proxies like Squid. You might need approval to download resources from the internet. This will be allowed only for official Linux repositories or dependency managers like Maven.</p>
<p>Most companies block public container registries like Docker Hub. So when you implement solutions, use private registries and official resources.</p>
<p>Create libraries and documents so anyone can onboard a new service without the knowledge of the tool.¬†</p>
<p>Some companies have platform teams who offer these generic templates as part of the <a data-id="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inner_source" data-type="link" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inner_source" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">InnerSource</a> efforts. </p>
<p>And different teams in an organization contribute to the InnerSource to make it better.</p>
<p>Develop pipeline libraries that everyone in the team understands. Just because you can create a complex library doesn‚Äôt mean you have to. Always think from a team perspective.</p>
<p>For example, you can create a shared library using <a data-id="5002" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/jenkins-pipeline-as-code/">Jenkins pipeline</a> DSL and pure Groovy code. <p>Every CI/CD tool has the concept of build agents. To save cost and separation of concerns, it‚Äôs good to leverage ephemeral build agents. Meaning the agents get deployed only when needed.</p>
<p>You can call them dynamic agents or on-demand agents.</p>
<p>Every build would be running on an agent from a specific template, and it ensures consistency in the build environments.</p>
<p>The ephemeral agent could be a VM, <a data-id="675" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/docker-containers-as-build-slaves-jenkins/">Docker container</a>, or even <a data-id="18305" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/kubernetes-pod/">Kubernetes pod</a>. Most CI/CD tools support ephemeral agents.</p>
<p>For example, you can integrate Jenkins with the <a data-id="4802" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/setup-kubernetes-cluster-kubeadm/">Kubernetes cluster</a> and configure jobs to spin up kubernetes pods as build agents.</p>
<p>GitHub actions by default support container-based agents or runners.</p>

<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Git est un syst√®me de contr√¥le de version distribu√© open source. Il est tr√®s l√©ger et fonctionne sur presque tous les syst√®mes d'exploitation.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">En 2005, Linus Torvalds a cr√©√© git comme syst√®me de contr√¥le de version distribu√© lorsque l'√©quipe de d√©veloppement du noyau Linux ne pouvait plus utiliser BitKeeper gratuitement.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Git est d√©sormais le syst√®me de contr√¥le de version de facto utilis√© par les d√©veloppeurs du monde entier. <p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Les r√©sultats </font></font><a data-id="https://insights.stackoverflow.com/survey" data-type="URL" href="https://insights.stackoverflow.com/survey" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">de l‚Äôenqu√™te aupr√®s des d√©veloppeurs StackOverflow</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> pr√©sent√©s ci-dessous montrent que </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">93 % des ing√©nieurs utilisent Git</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> et qu‚Äôil s‚Äôagit d‚Äôun outil fondamental pour eux.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Quand nous disons git, la plupart des nouveaux apprenants d‚Äôaujourd‚Äôhui font r√©f√©rence √† Github.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Des plateformes comme </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">GitHub ou Bitbucket</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> sont construites sur Git avec des fonctionnalit√©s suppl√©mentaires qui aident les ing√©nieurs et les organisations √† h√©berger et √† contr√¥ler les versions du code dans le r√©f√©rentiel Git distant. De plus, il est dot√© de bonnes int√©grations pour fonctionner avec d'autres outils CI/CD open source.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Avec GitHub Actions, vous pouvez configurer l'ensemble du pipeline CI/CD en utilisant les plateformes GitHub et Gitlab elles-m√™mes. Cela √©limine le besoin de g√©rer plusieurs outils pour CI/CD.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Examinons les facteurs cl√©s pour lesquels Git est n√©cessaire pour DevOps.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">L'une des t√¢ches d'un ing√©nieur DevOps est de </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">concevoir et de d√©velopper des pipelines CI/CD</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> . Git joue un r√¥le cl√© dans le CI/CD. D'apr√®s mon exp√©rience de travail dans diff√©rentes entreprises, je peux dire qu'il n'existe pas de norme unique pour la ramification et les flux de travail Git. Parfois, vous devez vous asseoir avec les d√©veloppeurs et discuter de la bonne approche pour la ramification Git dans le pipeline CI/CD. Cela inclut le balisage Git, la gestion des versions, etc.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">En fait, dans la plupart des organisations, les ing√©nieurs DevOps poss√®dent et exploitent les r√©f√©rentiels Git.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Ainsi, pour avoir une discussion significative avec les √©quipes de d√©veloppement, vous devez avoir une bonne connaissance de Git.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">De plus, lorsque nous parlons d' </font></font><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">infrastructure en tant que code</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> , nous d√©veloppons et maintenons tout le code d'infrastructure dans Git. Qu'il s'agisse d'un </font></font><a data-id="https://devopscube.com/jenkins-pipeline-as-code/" data-type="URL" href="https://devopscube.com/jenkins-pipeline-as-code/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">pipeline Jenkins</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> , d'un playbook Ansible ou d'un module Terraform.</font></font></p>
<p>We treat infra code the same way application code is treated. Meaning, infra code goes through the same unit testing and integration tests before getting deployed to any environment.</p>
<p>It means, even the infrastructure code needs to have a CI/CD pipeline. That again translates to git-based workflows.</p>
<p>Most companies do not follow test-driven development for infra code, but it is the standard way of developing infrastructure code.</p>
<p>With technical <strong>practices like GitOps</strong>, git acts as a source of truth for all the infrastructure configurations.</p>
<p>With Gitops, any change in git repo configs gets deployed in the infrastructure.</p>
<p>So it is a must for DevOps engineers to know all about git.</p>
<p>Also, tools like ArgoCD have the whole workflows around gitOps practice.</p>
<p>Here is the roadmap on how you can learn git.</p>

<p><strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Apprendre √† utiliser Kubernetes</font></font></strong><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> peut sembler compliqu√©. <p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Dans cette feuille de route d‚Äôapprentissage de Kubernetes, j‚Äôai ajout√© des pr√©requis et un parcours d‚Äôapprentissage complet qui couvre les concepts Kubernetes de base √† avanc√©s.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Avant de vous lancer dans l‚Äôapprentissage de Kubernetes, vous devez avoir une bonne connaissance de certaines des technologies et concepts sous-jacents.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Comprendre l'architecture de Kubernetes n'est pas une t√¢che facile. En apprenant l'architecture, vous rencontrerez les concepts que nous abordons dans les pr√©requis.</font></font></p>

<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Consultez le </font></font><a data-id="15162" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/kubernetes-architecture-explained/"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">guide d'architecture Kubernetes</font></font></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"> pour en savoir plus sur tous les composants Kubernetes en d√©tail.</font></font></p>
<p><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">Dans l‚Äôensemble, vous devez apprendre ce qui suit.</font></font></p>
<p><strong>Note</strong>: For DevOps interviews, ensure you have a very good understanding of Kubernetes architecture and how all the components interact with each other. </p>
<p>Deploying big clusters on the cloud could be expensive. So make use of the following cloud credits and learn to launch clusters <strong>as if you would on a real-time project</strong>. This will give you a sense of confidence in the process.</p>
<p>All platforms offer managed k8s services.</p>
<p>Use one account at a time. Once the credits have expired. move to the next account. You need to keep a watch on your credits as well as expiry. Or else you could get charged. Also, check the terms and instance usage limits if any.</p>
<p>Also, setting up servers on this platform is very easy and every cloud provider has extensive documentation to get started.</p>
<p>For <a data-id="1131" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/become-devops-engineer/">DevOps engineers</a>, it‚Äôs important to understand every component and cluster configuration. While there are many options to deploy a Kubernetes cluster, It is always better to learn to deploy multi-node clusters from scratch.</p>
<p>With multi-node clusters, you can learn about all the concepts like Cluster security, <a data-id="17820" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/kubernetes-high-availability/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">High Availability</a>, Scaling, Networking, etc.</p>
<p>It gives you the <strong>feeling of working on a real-world project</strong>. It will also help you in interviews and you can be confident about production-level cluster configurations.</p>
<p>Following are my cluster setup suggestions.</p>
<p>Once you have a working cluster, you should learn about the <strong>key cluster configurations</strong>. This knowledge will be particularly helpful when working in a self-hosted Kubernetes setup.</p>
<p>Even if you use a managed Kubernetes cluster for your project, there may be certain cluster configurations that you need to modify.</p>
<p>For example, if you set up a cluster in a hybrid network, you may need to configure it with an <strong>on-premises private DNS</strong> server for private DNS resolution. This can be done via CoreDNS configuration.</p>
<p><strong>Refer to the</strong>¬†<a href="https://devopscube.com/kubernetes-cluster-configurations/">Kubernetes Cluster configurations</a>¬†guide for more details.</p>
<p>Also, having a solid understanding of cluster configurations will help you with Kubernetes certifications (CKA &amp; CKS) where you need to troubleshoot cluster misconfiguration and issues.</p>
<p><strong><code>Kubeconfig</code></strong> file is a YAML file that contains all the cluster information and credentials to connect to the cluster. </p>
<p>As a Devops Engineer, You should learn to connect to kubernetes clusters in different ways using the Kubeconfig file. Because you will be responsible for setting up cluster <strong>authentication for CI/CD systems</strong>, providing cluster access to developers, etc.</p>
<p>So spend some time, understanding the Kubeconfig file structure and associated parameters.</p>
<p>Check out the <a data-id="13806" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/kubernetes-kubeconfig-file/">complete Kubeconfig file guide</a> to learn everything about the Kubeconfig file.</p>
<p>You will quite often come across the names ‚Äú<strong>Kubernetes Object</strong>‚Äù and ‚Äú<strong>Kubernetes Resource</strong>‚Äú</p>
<p>First, you need to Understand the difference between an object and a resource in kubernetes.</p>
<p>To put it simply, anything a <strong>user creates and persists in Kubernetes is an object</strong>. For example, a namespace, pod, Deployment configmap, Secret, etc.</p>
<p>Before creating an object, you represent it in a YAML or JSON format. It is called an <strong>Object Specification (Spec)</strong>. You declare the desired state of the object on the Object Spec. Once the object is created, you can retrieve its details from the Kubernetes API using Kubectl or client libraries.</p>
<p>As we discussed earlier in the prerequisite section, everything in Kubernetes is an API. To create different object types, there are <strong>API endpoints provided by the Kubernetes API server</strong>. Those <strong>object-specific api-endpoints are called resources</strong>. For example, an endpoint to create a pod is called a <strong>pod resource</strong>.</p>
<p>So when you try to create a Kubernetes Object using Kubectl, it converts the YAML spec to JSON format and sends it to the Pod resource (Pod API endpoint). </p>
<p>You can refer to the <a data-id="https://devopscube.com/kubernetes-objects-resources/" data-type="URL" href="https://devopscube.com/kubernetes-objects-resources/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">Kubernetes objects vs resource</a> guide for more details.</p>
<p>Once you have an understanding of Kubernetes Objects and resources, you can start with a native Kubernetes object called Pod. A pod is a basic building block of Kubernetes.</p>
<p>You should learn all the <strong>Pod concepts</strong> and their associated objects like <strong>Service, Ingress, Persistent Volume, Configmap, and Secret</strong>. Once you know everything about a pod, it is very easy to learn other pod-dependent objects like deployments, Daemonset, etc.</p>
<p>First, learn about the Pod Resource Definition (YAML). A typical Pod YAML contains the following high-level constructs.</p>
<p>Refer to <a data-id="18305" data-type="post" href="https://devopscube.com/kubernetes-pod/">Kubernetes Pod Explained</a> blog to learn all the basics about Pod.</p>
<p>Once you have a basic understanding of the above, move on to hands-on learning. These concepts will make more sense when you do hands-on.</p>
<p>Following are the <strong>hands-on tasks</strong> to learn about Pod and its associated objects. </p>
<p>Few advanced pod scheduling concepts.</p>
<p>Now that you have a better understanding of Pod and independent kubernetes resources, you can start learning about objects that are dependent on the Pod object. While learning this, you will come across concepts like HPA (Horizontal Pod Autoscaling) and VPA (Verification Pod Autoscaling)</p>
<p>To expose applications to the outside world or end users, kubernetes has a native object called ingress.</p>
<p>Many engineers get confused with Ingress due to less knowledge of Ingress controllers. Ensure you go through the concept of Ingress and Ingress controllers and understand it correctly. Because it is the base of exposing applications to the outside world.</p>
<p>You can start with the following comprehensive guides.</p>

<p>Once you understand the basics of these objects, you can try deploying an end-to-end microservices application on Kubernetes. Start with simple use cases and gradually increase complexity.</p>
